up by the price paid for electricity.
An overview of electricity prices paid by businesses for second half of 2016 published
by the Danish Energy Agency will be used to determine the current price level [79].
It is assumed that HOFOR District Cooling represents the category with a total
electricity use in the range from 2,000 to 20,000 MWh/year. For this category the
price is 271.00 DKK/MWh, which is the market price without taris and taxes.

According to the Danish rules on energy used for process purposes, the common
electricity tari can be repaid in some cases [81]. Some of the base load demand
at the customers in the DC system might be considered process cooling. But it is
found that the rules are strict and it might be dicult to document that the cooling
energy is solely used for process purposes. Hence, it is assumed that only electricity
used to drive the distributions pumps can be attributed a process purpose. This is
in line with the Danish legislation [86].
Price of cooling
The expected revenue is depending on the price that customers paid for cooling.
From a theoretical point of view the customer price for DC should reect the general
market for technical cooling solutions. A customer that decides to sign a contract for
DC obtains a number of benets, such as reduced risk, higher security of supply, less
43
==PAGE:60==
2.9. Economic analysis
space used for machinery etc. The theoretical price for DC can hence be formulated
as follows [87].
DC market price = Cost of customer′s local alternative + Added value
With this market oriented approach in mind it is recommended in literature that
customer contracts are created with individual pricing [7]. This thesis will not take
this into account but instead use a simplied approach on pricing.
Typically the price is composed of four components: Connection fee, xed fee, ca-
pacity fee, and energy fee [7]. For this analysis only the two last fees are included
for simplicity. List prices from the DC system in Thisted have been used as initial
price paid by customers [88]. The values are presented in table 2.15.

3.1
Possible locations for groundwater wells
Because of a densely built-up area and ongoing construction activities the free land
space for wells are quite limited in Ørestad. Furthermore, free space around the
edges of the case area is restricted due to drinking water interests as mentioned in
section 1.4.3 and protected nature zones to the west and the south. A free land
space is also available to the north-west, but a future residential area to be located
here excludes this option [47]. This means that groundwater wells for this case are
obliged to be placed within the case area or very close to the edges of the area. It
is assumed that only Ørestad City is appropriate for groundwater wells, due to the
northern location of the plant.
A number of suggested locations are given in gure 3.1, where the main criteria
have been free land without buildings and small distance to the expected DC system.
Especially the former criteria is important, due to the requirement for establishment
of a protection zone around wells.
In general, with the current plant site it is expected that locations 1 to 5 can be
part of a groundwater network connected to the plant. The initial expectation for
locations 6 to 8 is that these will only be feasible if they are implemented as pre-
cooling of DC return water right at the specic well site. A short description of the
individual locations seen in gure 3.1 will be given here.
Location 1 represents the available area for wells at the plant site. The options for
wells at this site might be limited due to the need for cooling machines and dry
coolers, but it is expected that one groundwater well can be located here.
Location 2 is a small grassy area which might be the site for one well, and if it turns
out that part of the adjacent parking lot can be used more than one well can be
located at this site.
Location 3 is an undeveloped area currently for sale for commercial buildings. To
place one well on the eastern edge (where the marker is put in gure 3.1) of this
land area seems to be realistic, and still allow for future commercial buildings on
the remaining part of the area. Naturally, this option requires a special agreement
with the authorities, since the land is for sale.
Location 4 is a narrow green area with no buildings. This location is actually located
just within the drinking water interests area (see section 1.4.3), but it is included
45
==PAGE:62==
3.1. Possible locations for groundwater wells
Figure 3.1: Potential locations for groundwater wells at the DC-plant and along the main distri-
bution line. The dark blue area is plant location and the red line is the expected main pipes in the
distribution network. Source: Google Earth.
here since it is located quite peripheral in the drinking water interest zone.
Location 5 and 6 are currently both undeveloped or used as parking lots, but both
land areas have been sold for commercial buildings, which are being planned at the
moment. Hence, it is expected that it will be dicult to obtain permissions for
groundwater wells at these locations.
Location 7 is a large park area for recreational purposes. With a lot of space, this
could be a suitable location for one or more groundwater wells.
Location 8 is an undeveloped land area currently for sale, and similar to location 3
it is expected that it is possible to make an agreement and buy a small corner of
the land for the wells.
When initiating a DC system from scratch in a new area it is recommended to start
with a small system and then expand regularly [35]. The planning of the ATES
system needs to follow this approach.
For instance if the rst phase of the DC
system only supplies cooling to customers north from e.g. location 5 in gure 2.2,
the return line pre-cooling wells at locations 6-8 would not be useful.
This leads to the conclusion that locations 1-5 are suitable for an initial phase of
the ATES system with a maximum distance to the plant of approximately 500 m.
It is assumed that these possible locations will lead to an initial construction of 4
wells, i.e. 2 well-pairs, with dedicated cold and hot well for each pair.
It is important to notice that this is only a preliminary screening and that further
detailed investigation is necessary before nal decisions with respect to sites for wells
can be made.

The dominating element in gure 3.2 is the extremely high COP-values for the free
cooler. It is seen that the highest peaks are generally grouped right before and
after the summer months. Figure 3.3 illustrates the cooling production divided on
contribution from free and mechanical cooling. It is evident that the free cooling

dierence is low for the free cooler at both sides, when it operates with with the
smallest load. Hence, these extreme COP values could be due to some unrealistic
situations occurring with the applied modelling approach.
The yearly variations of the chiller COP is seen to have lowest values in the summer
period, and higher values in the winter months, with a maximum of 13.3. This
is generally as expected, due to lower loads on the chiller and the possibility for
lower condensation pressure in the winter time. The plant overall COP follows the
chiller COP in the summer period, as the cooling production is almost exclusively
mechanical, as seen from gure 3.3. For the winter periods the overall COP decreases
as the free cooler COP increases, which means that the free cooler contribute less
to the overall COP in these situations.

3.2.3
Groundwater used continuously
The second ATES scenario is the continuous operation where the groundwater is
used for cooling for every hour in a specied period. As shown in gure 3.9 the
COP of the ATES technology is varying between a minimum COP of around 8 to
a maximum of 26, when groundwater cooling is activated. With comparison to the
COP-values for the reference system (gure 3.2), it is seen that fewer extreme values
of the free cooler COP is present in the beginning and end of the ATES operation
period. Another thing worth noticing, is that the chiller COP is slightly above the
COP for the overall plant in the summer period.

3.2.4
Groundwater used as a condenser heat carrier
The third operation scenario for the ATES system is the removal of condenser heat.
This method scenario is characterised by supplying no direct cooling energy to the
DC distribution system, but instead it is intended to improve the chiller performance
and lower the dry cooler load. Two dierent groundwater extraction ow rates are
investigated. The case with the lower values is expected to be the most realistic,
with respect to how much cooling load the aquifer can supply with its physical
properties. The COP-values for the overall plant and the chiller are shown in gure
3.11. The ATES condenser heat operation occurs from May to August, i.e. from
around hour number 2900 to around 5900.

It is evident from the gures that the ATES system is not capable of carrying all
condenser heat. This is also why the period of operation has not been extended
to more than 4 months. It is seen from gure 3.12 that a few very high condenser
heat loads occur immediately after the active period of the ATES operation. If it is
assumed that these peaks can also be covered by the ATES system, the maximum
necessary installed capacity of dry coolers is 5953 kW for the low groundwater ex-
traction ow rate case and 5080 kW for the high case. Table 3.4 shows the results
for the two considered condenser heat variants.
Note that the ATES COP does not make sense for this scenario, due to the fact
that no direct cooling is supplied from the groundwater. In comparison with the
reference system, both of the considered condenser heat cases improve the yearly
chiller COP. On the other hand, the yearly overall COP is decreased. This is mainly
due to the extra pumping power needed for recharge operation.
In the high ow rate case 89.3% of the condenser heat is deposited in the aquifer.
Still it is necessary to install 5080 kW of dry cooler capacity, i.e. a decrease of 34%
in the installed dry cooler capacity compared to the reference system. For the low
ow case the decrease in dry cooler capacity is 22.7%.

be used at times where the cooling demand is low. Looking only at the cooling oper-

models. In contrast to free cooling with air, the ground water is used in the summer
where a high COP is more likely to make a dierence on a yearly basis. This is

continuous operation scenarios, in comparison with the reference system.
Based on the simulation results, the condenser heat scenario is the least attractive
of the investigated operation methods for the DC system in this specic case. Its
yearly overall COP is lower than for the reference system, because of too many extra
hours of operation when the aquifer is recharged. On the other hand, this operation
method shows to improve the yearly chiller COP. The condenser heat scenario might
come to its right if the system is equipped with a heat pump, so that the stored
energy in the aquifer is actually utilised for heating purposes in the winter period.

presented in this section. Based on the economic indicators the most economically
attractive solution can be identied.

the total initial investment, and the xed part of O&M costs are shown in table 3.6.
The peak load case with a limit of 1500 kW, and the condenser heat case with low
ow rates are applied in this economic analysis.

The results for the PBT indicate that the reference system is of primary interest
with a value of 5.1 years. Of the three ATES scenarios, the continuous operation is
the best option with respect to the time for recovering the initial investment. with
5.4 years. The peak load operation is almost as attractive with a value of 5.5 years.
The higher value for the condenser heat operation scenario is primarily due to the
higher initial investment costs.
56
==PAGE:73==
Chapter 3. Results
The private-economic NPV is highest for the reference system with 14.90 million
DKK, which is closely followed by the ATES peak load operation scenario with an
NPV of 14.49 million DKK. Next is the continuous operation of ATES with 13.06
million DKK, and nally the condenser heat operation scenario with 1.51 million
DKK. The results for the IRR follows the trend of the NPV, with the highest IRR of
13.0% for the reference system and the lowest for the ATES condenser heat scenario
which is 8.4%.
As seen from table 3.7 the PI values support the trends found for the private NPV
and IRR. The ranking of the project alternatives from a private-economic perspective
is hence:
1. Reference system
2. ATES peak load
3. ATES continuous
4. ATES condenser heat
It should also be noted that all project alternatives have PI > 1, NPV > 0 and
IRR > discount rate. This means that they are all worth pursuing, but because
they are here considered to be mutually exclusive the one with the highest PI should
be preferred.
Overall, the results presented here show that DC systems with integrated ATES are
inferior to the reference system when it comes to economics. The lower capacities
required for chiller and/or dry coolers for the ATES scenarios are not enough to beat
the conventional technology on the costs. This is due to higher investment and xed
O&M costs as seen in table 3.6. Comparing the three ATES scenarios it is clear that
condenser heat operation is the least attractive to invest in. The PBT indicates that
the continuous scenario is best among the three, but the PBT is in its nature a short
term indicator. Instead, when considering the PI, the peak load scenario provides
the most attractive investment opportunity between the three ATES options.
3.4
Parameter variations
3.4.1
Number of well-pairs for the ATES system
One of the main assumptions that frames the investigations presented in this thesis
is the number of well-pairs to be used in the ATES system. In order to investigate
the inuence of this assumption, a small study is made to see if the conclusions are
dierent in case the number of well-pairs is increased. Since the ATES peak load
scenario is found to be the best option among the three suggested, this scenario is
put in focus for this parameter variation analysis.
Table 3.8 shows the main simulation results for the ATES peak load scenario (peak
limit 1500 kW), for three dierent number of well-pairs. The assumptions on ground-
water extraction ow rates per well-pair are unchanged, so this analysis can be
considered an investigation of the available ATES cooling capacity. The reference
system results are included for comparison.
As expected, it is seen that the necessary chiller and dry cooler capacity is decreased
with the number of wells. At the same time the ATES COP is decreasing as more

between 2 and 3 well-pairs is small, and the PBT for these two cases are equal. The
reference system is still the most attractive from an economical point of view.

The results of the price-variation shows that the PI-graphs for the reference system
and the ATES peak load scenario are crossing at increased electricity prices. If the
price is increased to above 37.4%, corresponding to a price of 2156 DKK/MWh or
2.16 DKK/kWh in the rst year of operation, the peak load scenario will be more
economically feasible than the reference system.
The same investigation made for the private NPV shows that the peak scenario and
reference reaches the same level when the electricity price is increased by 19.1%,
corresponding to a price of 1869 DKK/MWh or 1.87 DKK/kWh.

3.4. Parameter variations
60
==PAGE:77==
Chapter 4
Discussion
The parameter variation of the number of well-pairs to be installed at the plant
indicates an optimum of 3 well-pairs for the considered DC system, operated after a
peak load scheme. The investigation of number of possible wells in the case area is a
very preliminary study, and it is necessary to conduct a more detailed investigation
of the possibilities for well locations in the area. In reality, it might be the case that
many barriers needs to be crossed before the groundwater wells for an ATES system
can become reality. Especially the characterisation of the aquifer is needed, in order
to arrange the hot and cold wells most optimally for this specic case, where cooling
is the main purpose.
The results from the thermodynamic simulations shows that the peak load operation
is the most attractive of the three dierent ATES scenarios. This scenario is also
the one with the highest extraction groundwater ow rates applied. The dierent
ow rates for each system are justied from a realistic approach, taking into account
that the physical limitations of the aquifer should be respected in order to maintain
a viable operation of the ATES system for many years. The higher ow rates for
the peak scenario might be said to pre-favour this system operation method. On the
other hand, the ow rates are determined on the basis of data and experience from
existing ATES systems, which suggest that the approach used here is appropriate.
The chiller cycle has been modelled on the basis of an assumed isentropic compressor
eciency. The assumed value of 0.70 is within the range of typical values stated for
large scale open compressors used in ammonia systems. However, the compressor
constitutes a major share of the total energy consumption, e.g. 72% for the ref-
erence system on a yearly basis. Hence, this parameter can possibly inuence the
yearly plant simulation results signicantly. Application of appropriate compressor
polynomials to the simulation models could improve the validity of the results. The
ndings of this thesis should hence be seen in the light of the lack of detail level
with respect to the isentropic compressor eciency.
The dry cooler capacity is reduced the most under the condenser heat scenario. With
a minimum necessary capacity of 5080 kW among the investigated ATES scenarios,
it is clear that integration of district cooling and ATES under the given conditions
require a considerable amount of dry cooler capacity. By increasing the capacity
of groundwater cooling from an ATES system, the amount of dry cooler capacity
necessary in the cooling season is decreased. But this will lead to higher amounts
of recharge in the winter period, which will again require more dry cooler capacity.
61
==PAGE:78==
From this, it could be argued that in cases with a requirement for yearly energy
balance in the aquifer, the ATES technology serves best for thermal energy systems
where both the cold and the hot energy is utilised, because of less required dry
cooler capacity and less "wasted" energy for fans/pump under recharge. On the
other hand it is found that the yearly COP for the DC plant can be increased if
groundwater cooling is used for peak load.
The common brine loop on the dry cooler side of the plant is in this thesis assumed
to let the electricity consumption of each technology relate to the total installed
capacity of the dry coolers. With the applied relations for fans and pumps some
unrealistic COP values appear for the free cooler at low cooling loads. Figure 4.1
shows the fan power as a function of ambient temperature. The fan power is very
close to zero when the operation is free or combi cooling.

Figure 4.1: Fan power as a function of ambient temperature. Left: Full range of temperatures,
right: Zoom to combi cooling interval.
Even though the fans are speed controlled there might in reality be a lower limit to
their operation, and the behaviour would then be similar to xed speed fans when
the variable speed fans reaches their lower limit. In this case you would expect
the free cooling to come to a stop as the fans are completely shut of. It would thus
maybe be unrealistic for the fans to operated at the low power consumptions evident
from the right plot in gure 4.1. The EES-model constructed for this work does not
take this into account, and it might be the reason for the extreme COP-values for
the free cooler.
The methodology for modelling the heat exchangers for air based free cooling and
the groundwater cooling/recharge, is made with a pinch point approach with a
pinch dened as ∆T = 2.5◦C in all the involved exchanger components.
Other
investigations is later found to use a temperature dierence of 1◦C for groundwater
exchanger, which makes the current investigation conservative.
The electricity price projection applied in the economic analysis is suggesting steadily
increasing prices. There are dierent opinions on the development of the electricity
price, and it might as well decrease over the next 20 years. The inputs to the eco-
nomic calculations are based on typical values from the tool for assessing district
cooling projects. However, the economic calculation could be improved by using
updated values, possibly based on experience from similar projects with DC and/or
ATES.
62
==PAGE:79==
Chapter 5
Conclusion
The initial investigation of the groundwater availability and ATES systems in the
case area showed that groundwater can normally be expected to yield 50-100 m3/h
per well-pair in an ATES system. The groundwater temperature for the case area
is found to vary ±0.5◦C around an average value of 10.27◦C .
A demand curve for the DC system has been constructed on the basis of an appro-
priate mix of customer types for the case area over a full year. The hourly demand
shows a maximum of 5910 kW, and the base load is calculated to be 450 kW.
The yearly thermodynamic simulations have showed that the combination of a DC
system and the ATES technology is optimally utilised when groundwater is used at
peak cooling demand. Dierent denitions of peak demand has been investigated
in the range 1500 kW to 4000 kW. Generally the COPtot,year of the overall system
is higher the lower the denition of peak demand. For the case where the ATES
system supply cooling at demands above 1500 kW, the yearly overall COP is found
to be 5.57 in the base situation with 2 groundwater well-pairs available. This is an
improvement in comparison with the reference system that shows a yearly overall
COP of 5.08.
A parameter variation has indicated that the considered DC system is optimised on
a yearly basis, if 3 well-pairs are installed. In this case it is found that COPtot,year =
5.64 and the
The yearly overall COP of the continuous operation is found to be 5.11, which
is slightly above the reference system.
For the condenser heat operation of the
ATES system, the yearly chiller COP is improved to 5.03 and 5.04, for the low
( ˙Vgw,cool = 50m3/h) and high groundwater extraction ow rates ( ˙Vgw,cool = 75m3/h),
respectively. It is seen that the inuence of increasing the ow rate is minimal for
the chiller COP. The overall COP for the condenser heat low and high ow cases
are 4.73 and 4.59, respectively.
The reference system is the more economically attractive option among the consid-
ered system scenarios. This is in spite of a lower yearly electricity in the peak load
and the continuous operation scenarios. The private-economic NPV is calculated
to be 14.90 million DKK for the reference system, 14.49 million DKK for the peak
scenario, 13.06 million DKK for the continuous scenario, and nally 1.77 million
DKK for the condenser heat scenario. The higher costs for ATES installations over-
63
==PAGE:80==
shadows the benets of lower electricity consumption and lower requirements for
dry cooler and chiller capacity.
The electricity savings are 9.9% for the ATES peak scenario with 1500 kW peak
demand limit, whereas for the continuous scenario the savings is only 0.6%. The
condenser heat electricity use is 7.3% higher than the value for the reference system.
These conclusions suggest that an ATES system is viable from the energy perspec-
tive, when dimensioned in accordance with a primary purpose of peak load operation.
From an economical perspective the ATES technology is not feasible, and the reason
for choosing the ATES system should be energy savings.
For future work within the subject covered in this thesis, it would be interesting to
look at the ATES scenarios in more details, for a possible optimisation of an DC-
ATES plant with multiple ATES operation modes included in the operation scheme.
Further investigations are also needed with respect to the isentropic eciency of the
compressor in the chillers. The combination of DC and ATES could potentially
also benet from using heat pumps in the winter operation, for utilisation of energy
released from the aquifer under recharge operation.

Appendix A
Investigation of groundwater and
ATES
A.1
Legislative conditions for groundwater installa-
tions
One of the advantages of ATES systems is the limited space requirement at ground
level.
The common practice is to create the wells as vertical boreholes in order
to reach the appropriate depth most eciently. After installing the underground
equipment (such as pumps, piping, sealing liner etc.) the drilling is nalised with a
well-top housing in which valves, meters, coupling to horizontal transport pipes etc.
are to be placed. The top housing is normally countersunk under the terrain level
to limit visual impact, at the expense of higher costs and increased inconvenience in
relation to maintenance work etc. Certain sealing techniques should be applied at
ground level in order to prevent seepage of surface water to the groundwater layers
and potential contamination. The terrain around the well-top housing should be
raised to at least 0.2 m above normal terrain level, and the upper edge of the housing
should be at least 0.3 m above the new elevated ground level [44]. In addition, the
upper edge of the housing should be locate above the expected maximum water level
in from nearby rivers, lakes etc.
The extent of ground level installations at the drilling site might be case specic,
but in general the needed equipment at this location is limited. On the other hand,
it is important that good access to the well-top housing exists for inspections, main-
tenance and measurements. The housing should be at least 1.5 m in diameter and
possess a ladder if the construction is countersunk under the surface [44]. In addi-
tion, cases can occur where it is necessary to lay out a concrete layer within 2 m
distance around the top housing, which is inclined away from the well.
According to the rules on execution of groundwater boreholes and wells it is required
that a protection zone can be established within a 5 m radius circular area around
the well location [43]. This is the requirement stated for non-public water supply,
and it is found to be reasonable that this also applies for wells with the purpose of
thermal utilisation of the groundwater.
75
==PAGE:92==
A.2. Pre-investigation for ATES projects
A.2
Pre-investigation for ATES projects
This section will describe dierent elements normally included in a pre-investigation
for a desired ATES system at a specic site. This will be based on ndings from
literature and a specic pre-investigation plan oered to HOFOR District Cooling by
a commercial company with specialisation in subsurface investigation and technology
[36,46,47].
Initially, it should be mentioned that some legal requirements for documentation
that needs to be attached in the authority application [45]. The pre-investigation
normally includes the creation of this documentation, which should include the
following.
1. Groundwater is extracted and injected into the same aquifer.
2. Studies have been conducted that provide information about:
a) the geology and extent of the aquifer (horizontal as well as vertical),
b) the hydraulic characteristics of the groundwater reservoir, including hy-
draulic contact with other aquifers,
c) the hydrogeological conditions of the aquifer,
d) the chemistry and microbiology of the aquifer, and
e) hydrothermal properties of the groundwater reservoir.
An enterprise that considers and initiates the planning of an ATES system is facing
a large economic risk. This is due to the fact that the pre-investigation itself can
typically cost more than 1 million DKK [47], and all the way through this initial work
there is no certainty that the project is feasible to put into practice. In that case the
money and resources spend will lead to no prot/benet for the company, other than
nding that this ATES system is not possible or feasible at the investigated location.
If the pre-investigation is arranged to be divided in phases, it the economical loss
might be limited since only the initial part of the pre-investigation should be paid
for.
An example of a phase divided pre-investigation is provided in table A.1.
This
division of phases is used by the subsurface company GEO.
Table A.1: Example of phase divided pre-investigation program for ATES [47].
Phase
number
Description
Probability after the
phase is nalised [%]
1
Initial screening and authority contact
70
2
Establishment of survey drilling
75
3
Acidication of drilling, geophysical
logging and pumping test
80
4
Groundwater modelling
90
5
Documentation, reporting and application
95
The probabilities provided in the rightmost column are the company's estimates
for the likelihood that the project will be realised after a positive outcome of the
given phase. The purpose of the authority contact in phase 1 is to initiate an early
dialogue with municipality etc.
to identify requirements and important aspects
76
==PAGE:93==
Appendix A. Investigation of groundwater and ATES
to include in the applications. Initial screening refers to investigating all relevant
existing material and data from the area.
Phase 2 and 3 is related to test drilling and sampling, to identify the properties that
characterises the aquifer. Some of these data will be included in the application to
authorities, and some test data will be used as inputs for the groundwater modelling
in phase 4.
Existing groundwater models (e.g. developed under investigations for earlier drilling
projects close to the site) are to be used as a basis in phase 4. With input data from
phase 3, the modelling will be rened for the specic site. One of the purposes is
to identify thermal propagation and possible breakthrough times with the intended
operation scheme suggested by the future operator of the ATES system. This will
help in designing the well-pair layout, i.e. locations for cold and hot wells.
For a more detailed description of aquifer characterisation and pre-investigation,
please refer to the paper by Bridger & Allen (2005) [46].
A.3
Expected natural groundwater temperatures
The aim of this thesis is to conduct yearly simulations and hence it is desired to
achieve data with an hourly or daily resolution, preferably for a full year.
It is
expected that the simulation model will yield more accurate results if the potential
seasonal changes of the natural groundwater temperature is taken into account. For
this purpose, two primary types of data-sources have been investigated:
1. Measurements from existing ATES systems (locations near the case area are
preferred)
2. Measurements from wells in existing water supply systems (restricted to loca-
tions on Amager)
It is desired to obtain and use these groundwater temperature data in a high reso-
lution, in order to enhance the accuracy of the simulation model.
The initial investigation of existing ATES systems included the following locations:
 Copenhagen Towers Crowne Plaza
 Rambøll Headquarters
 DR-Byen
 CPH Airport
 DTU Risø
 Bispebjerg Hospital
Little or no information on the groundwater temperature have been available from
most of the above systems. In some cases, an external company operates the system
and thus handles the data acquisition, which makes it problematic to obtain the
desired information. Other systems are found to have problems with their monitor-
ing and data storage systems, so that the desired temperature data is unavailable.
Lastly, some of the system owners are not interested in contributing with information
on their system.
77
==PAGE:94==
A.4. Expected extraction ow rates in the ATES system
The literature is similarly found to provide little information on the temperature of
the groundwater. A database with information from groundwater wells in Denmark
is available online [52]. Due to the lack of information from actual ATES systems,
the Jupiter database is investigated and found to be the most appropriate source
of information under the given circumstances. The database is used to investigate
groundwater wells located close to the case area.
Hence, only wells located on
Amager are included. It is desired that the frequency of measurements are as high
as possible. Also, typical ATES systems have wells in the depth range 80-100 meters,
and hence deep wells are preferred. Measurements from wells of smaller depths might
provide sucient results, because groundwater temperature is generally stated to
have little variations in depths below 5 meters under terrain level.
A.4
Expected extraction ow rates in the ATES
system
The presence of a subterranean fault zone/line close to the bottom of a groundwater
well might signicantly increase the yield, i.e. the extracted groundwater ow rate
to be pumped to the heat exchanger. A fault zone tends to increase the natural
occurring groundwater ow within the aquifer, and hence the aquifer around the
extraction well will be harder to 'drain'. On the other hand, the storage possibilities
of an ATES system tends to vanish in this case.
A possible large horizontally
and natural occurring groundwater ow within the aquifer, would imply that the
thermal energy intended to be stored from season to season would be carried away
and dispersed downstream from the well.
Conditions in existing systems on are investigated to nd out what extraction
groundwater ow rate can be expected in the case area.
The same systems as
listed for the temperature investigation (see appendix A.3) have been contacted for
this information on ow rates. To some degree, the outcomes are similar: Many op-
erators either cannot or do not want to inform about the measurements from their
plant for this thesis.
78

// Subprogam for free cooling HEX (operation mode: free cooling).
Subprogram freehex(Tairfree_in;Tdcfree_in;Pdc_in;Tset;mdc;cpair_in;mairfree_in:Tdc_out_final;cpdc_in;Qdot_free;
Tairfree_out)
$UpdateGuesses
"Mediums"
D$ = 'water'
"Air side"
Qdot_free = mairfree_in * cpair_in * (Tairfree_out - Tairfree_in)
"DC water inlet"
cpdc_in = cp(D$;T=Tdcfree_in;P=Pdc_in)
"Specific heat capacity of DC inlet water"
"DC water outlet"
Qdot_free = mdc * cpdc_in * (Tdcfree_in - Tset)
"Temperature based heat transfer rate, based on 
DC-side"
Tdc_out_final = Tset
"Assigning output-value for DC-out state"
End
 
// Subprogam for free cooling HEX and chiller cycle (operation mode: combi).
Subprogram freehexchiller(Taircond_in;Tairfree_in;Tcond;UAevap;mdc;Tdcfree_in;Pdc_in;etacomp;dTsc;dTsh;Tset;
cpair_in;mairfree_in;maircond_in;Tdc_inter;xevap_out;dp_sl;etamotor:Qdot_cond;Taircond_out;DELTAT_1evap;Tevap;
DELTAT_2evap;DELTAT_CMevap;Qdot_evap;Pevap;Tsuction;Psuction;hsuction;ssuction;Pdischarge;sisdischarge;
hisdischarge;hdischarge;Tdischarge;mrefrigerant;hcondensate;Wdot_comp;Pratio;Pcond;Tcondensate;Pcondensate;
Texpand;Pexpand;hexpand;Tdcevap_out;cpdcevap_out;hevap_out;ncirc;Tevap_out;Pevap_out;mevap;hevap_sat_l;
hevap_sat_v;Tevap_sat_l;Pevap_sat_l;Tevap_sat_v;Pevap_sat_v)
$UpdateGuesses
"Mediums"
RE$ = 'Ammonia'
D$ = 'Water'
 
"! *_*_*_*_*_*_*_* Free cooler *_*_*_*_*_*_*_*"
"Free cooler calculations for combi mode are moved outside the subprogram. Find the equations in procedure 
activecomponents."
 
"! *_*_*_*_*_*_*_*_* Chiller *_*_*_*_*_*_*_*_*_*"
"Condenser air inlet"
Qdot_cond = maircond_in * cpair_in * (Taircond_out-Taircond_in) 
"Eq. for condenser heat gives the brine temp. after 
condenser"
"Evaporator"
DELTAT_1evap = Tdc_inter - Tevap
"Temperature difference, hot end"
DELTAT_2evap = Tdcevap_out - Tevap
"Temperature difference, cold end"
"Chen mean (CMTD)"
DELTAT_CMevap = (1/2*DELTAT_1evap^0,3275 + 1/2*DELTAT_2evap^0,3275)^(1/0,3275)
Qdot_evap = UAevap * DELTAT_CMevap
Pevap = pressure(RE$;T=Tevap;x=1)
"Evaporation 
pressure defined from refrigerant saturated state"
hevap_out = enthalpy(RE$;T=Tevap;x=xevap_out)
"Enthalpy of refrigerant out of evaporator (
assumed quality <1 for the flooded evaporator)"
ncirc = 1/xevap_out
"Circulation number in flooded evaporator"
Tevap_out = Tevap
"Temperature out of the evaporator corresponds to 
evaporation temperature"
Pevap_out = Pevap
"Pressure out of the evaporator corresponds to 
evaporation temperature"
"Low pressure receiver"
hevap_sat_l = enthalpy(RE$;T=Tevap;x=0)
"Enthapy of saturated liquid in the receiver"
Tevap_sat_l = Tevap
Pevap_sat_l = Pevap
hevap_sat_v = enthalpy(RE$;T=Tevap;x=1)
"Enthapy of saturated vapor in the receiver"
Tevap_sat_v = Tevap
Pevap_sat_v = Pevap
Qdot_evap = mevap/ncirc * (hevap_sat_v - hevap_sat_l)
"Equation for heat rate in flooded evaporator gives 
the actual mass flow of liquid refrigerant in the evaporator"
"Compressor suction side"
==PAGE:99==
File:Reference system.EES
31-05-2017 18:31:26  Page 2
EES Ver. 10.207: #0780: Department of Energy Engineering, Tech. Univ. of Denmark
Tsuction = Tevap_out + dTsh
"Temperature before compressor - super heat is 
unuseful (supplied to the refrigerant in suction line from compressor heat etc.)"
Psuction = Pevap - dp_sl
"Pressure before compressor equals evaporation 
pressure minus assumed pressure loss in suction line"
hsuction = enthalpy(RE$;T=Tsuction;P=Psuction)
"Enthalpy of superheated refrigerant after 
evaporator"
ssuction = entropy(RE$;T=Tsuction;P=Psuction)
"Entropy before compressor"
"Compressor discharge side"
Pdischarge = Pcond
"Comp. applies a press. rise corresp. to necessary 
cond. pressure"
sisdischarge = ssuction
"Isentropic compression"
hisdischarge = enthalpy(RE$;s=sisdischarge;P=Pdischarge) 
"Enthalpy in the case of isentropic compression"
etacomp = (hisdischarge-hsuction)/(hdischarge-hsuction) 
"Expression for isentropic efficiency used to 
dertermine actual enthalpy after compressor."
Tdischarge = temperature(RE$;h=hdischarge;P=Pdischarge) 
"Refrigerant temperature out of condenser"
Qdot_cond = mrefrigerant * (hdischarge - hcondensate)
"Calculation of heat rejection in the condenser"
Wdot_comp = mrefrigerant * (hdischarge - hsuction)/etamotor
"Compressor power"
Pratio = Pdischarge/Psuction
"Pressure ratio"
"Condensate out of condenser"
Pcond = pressure(RE$;T=Tcond;x=1) 
"Condensation pressure"
Tcondensate = Tcond - dTsc
"Refrigerant temp. out of condenser is cond. temp. 
minus subcool."
Pcondensate = Pcond
"Refrigerant press. out of condenser is the cond. 
pressure"
hcondensate = enthalpy(RE$;T=Tcondensate;P=Pcondensate) 
"Enthalpy out of the condenser"
"Expanded condensate before evaporator"
Texpand = Tevap
"Refrigerant temp. into evaporator is the 
evaporation temp."
Pexpand = Pevap
"Refrigerant pressure into evaporator is the 
evaporation pressure"
hexpand = hcondensate
"Isenthalpic expansion: Enthalpy is unchanged 
over the exp. valve"
Qdot_evap = mrefrigerant * (hsuction - hexpand)
"Eq. for energy transfer in the evaporator gives 
mass flow on refrigerant side"
"DC water after evaporator"
Tdcevap_out = Tset
"Chiller production controlled from setpoint DC 
supply temp."
cpdcevap_out = cp(D$;T=Tdcevap_out;P=Pdc_in)
"Specific heat of of chilled water out of evaporator"
Qdot_evap = mdc * cpdcevap_out * (Tdc_inter - Tdcevap_out) 
"Calculation of required cooling delivered by 
evaporator"
 
End

//______________________________________ PROCEDURES _________________________________________
//*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-
 
// Procedure for definition of operation mode. Inputs: 'x'=determining temperature, 'tlow'=low operation mode limit, 'thigh'=
high operation mode limit, 'a'=first operation mode number, 'b'=second operation mode number, 'c'=third operation mode 
number. Output: 'name'=variable name of the (numeric) operation mode number. 
Procedure plantoperation(x;tlow;thigh;a;b;c:name)
If (x <= tlow) Then
"Free cooling"
name := a
==PAGE:101==
File:Reference system.EES
31-05-2017 18:31:26  Page 4
EES Ver. 10.207: #0780: Department of Energy Engineering, Tech. Univ. of Denmark
Else
"Combi cooling"
If (x <= thigh) Then
name := b
Else
"Mechanical cooling"
name := c
Endif
Endif
End
 
// Procedure that contains a condition for which components to be active in the cooling plant. The relevant subprograms 
are called according to the operation mode.
Procedure activecomponents(opmode;T[16];T[31];P[31];T_setpoint;m_dot_dist;cp_air;m_dot_16;T[10];T_cond;UA_evap;
eta_comp;DELTAT_sc;DELTAT_sh;m_dot_10;T[41];P[41];C_hot_free;C_cold_free;x_evap_out;DELTAp_sl;
eta_motor_comp:cp_31;Q_dot_free;T[17];T[32];Q_dot_cond;T[11];DELTAT_1_evap;DELTAT_2_evap;T_evap;
DELTAT_CM_evap;Q_dot_evap;P_evap;T[1];P[1];h[1];s_1;P[2];s_2_s;h_2_s;h[2];T[2];m_dot_r;h[3];W_dot_comp;P_rat;
P_cond;T[3];P[3];T[4];P[4];h[4];T[42];cp_42;h[6];n_circ;T[6];P[6];m_dot_evap;h[5];h[7];T[5];P[5];T[7];P[7])
 
If (opmode = 1) Then
"Free cooling"
Call freehex(T[16];T[31];P[31];T_setpoint;m_dot_dist;cp_air;m_dot_16:T[32];cp_31;Q_dot_free;T[17])
Q_dot_cond := 0
T[11] := T[10]
DELTAT_1_evap := 12,5
DELTAT_2_evap := 2
T_evap := 0
DELTAT_CM_evap := 5,725359747
Q_dot_evap := 0
P_evap := 4
T[1] := 5,5
P[1] := 4
h[1] := 0
s_1 := 0
P[2] := 8
s_2_s := 0
h_2_s := 0
h[2] := 0
T[2] := 20
m_dot_r := 0
h[3] := 0
W_dot_comp := 0
P_rat := 2
P_cond := 8
T[3] := 20
P[3] := 8
T[4] := 10
P[4] := 4
h[4] := 0
T[42] := 10
cp_42 := 4,183
h[6] := 0
n_circ:= 0
T[6] := 5,5
P[6] := 4
m_dot_evap := 0
h[5] := 0
h[7] = 0
T[5] := 0
P[5] := 0
T[7] := 0
P[7] := 0
Else
"Combi cooling"
If (opmode = 2) Then
If (C_hot_free<=C_cold_free) Then
"If C_dc < C_air 
then the pinch is at DC water outlet."
T[32] := T[16] + 2,5[C]

31-05-2017 18:31:26  Page 5
EES Ver. 10.207: #0780: Department of Energy Engineering, Tech. Univ. of Denmark
cp_31 := 4,183[kJ/kg-K]
Q_dot_free := m_dot_dist * cp_31 * (T[31] - T[32])
T[17] := Q_dot_free / (m_dot_16 * cp_air) + T[16]
Else
"If C_dc > C_air then the pinch is at the DC water 
inlet."
T[17] := T[31] - 2,5[C]
cp_31 := 4,183[kJ/kg-K]
Q_dot_free := m_dot_16 * cp_air * (T[17] - T[16])
T[32] := T[31] - Q_dot_free / (m_dot_dist * cp_31)
Endif
 
Call freehexchiller(T[10];T[16];T_cond;UA_evap;m_dot_dist;T[31];P[31];eta_comp;DELTAT_sc;DELTAT_sh;T_setpoint;
cp_air;m_dot_16;m_dot_10;T[32];x_evap_out;DELTAp_sl;eta_motor_comp:Q_dot_cond;T[11];DELTAT_1_evap;T_evap;

P[7])
 
Else
"Mechanical cooling"
Call chiller(m_dot_10;cp_air;T[10];T[41];UA_evap;DELTAT_sh;eta_comp;DELTAT_sc;T_setpoint;P[41];m_dot_dist;
T_cond;x_evap_out;DELTAp_sl;eta_motor_comp:Q_dot_cond;T[11];DELTAT_1_evap;T[42];DELTAT_2_evap;T_evap;

P_cond;T[3];P[3];T[4];P[4];h[4];cp_42;h[6];n_circ;T[6];P[6];m_dot_evap;h[5];h[7];T[5];P[5];T[7];P[7])
T[32] := 20
cp_31 := 4,183
Q_dot_free := 0
T[17] := T[16]
Endif
Endif
End
 
// Procedure for correct flow configuration of DC water according to the operation mode. 'final' refers to the state right 
before distribution pumps.
Procedure dcflowconfig(opmode;mdc_ret;Tdc_ret;Tdc_final;Tdcfree_out;Pdc_ret;mode1$;Tdc_precool:mdcGWHEX1;
mdcfree_in;mdcbuffer_in;mdcbuffer_out;mdcevap_in;mdcfinal;TdcGWHEX1_in;Tdcfree_in;Tdcbuffer_in;Tdcbuffer_out;

If (opmode = 1) Then
"! Statements for operation mode 1"
"Mass flow rates"
If (mode1$ = 'on') Then
mdcGWHEX1 := mdc_ret
Else
mdcGWHEX1 := 0
Endif
mdcfree_in := mdc_ret
mdcbuffer_in := mdcfree_in
mdcbuffer_out :=mdcbuffer_in

mdcfinal := mdcbuffer_out
 
"Temperatures"
If (mode1$ = 'on') Then
TdcGWHEX1_in := Tdc_ret
Tdcfree_in := Tdc_precool
Else
TdcGWHEX1_in := 999
Tdcfree_in := Tdc_ret
Endif
Tdcbuffer_in := Tdcfree_out
Tdcbuffer_out := Tdcbuffer_in
Tdcevap_in := 0
"Pressures"
Pdcfree_in := Pdc_ret
Pdcbuffer_in := Pdcfree_in
Pdcbuffer_out := Pdcbuffer_in
Pdcevap_in := 1
Else
If (opmode = 2) Then
"! Statements for operation mode 2"

"Mass flow rates"
If (mode1$ = 'on') Then
mdcGWHEX1 := mdc_ret
Else
mdcGWHEX1 := 0
Endif
mdcfree_in := mdc_ret
mdcbuffer_in := 0
mdcbuffer_out := 0
mdcevap_in := mdcfree_in
mdcfinal := mdcevap_in
 "Temperatures"
If (mode1$ = 'on') Then
TdcGWHEX1_in := Tdc_ret

// Procedure for different necessary operational measures, including air temp. into the exchangers
Procedure control(opmode;mode1$;mode2$;Tair;dTdry;dTcond;Tcondmin;Tfreemin;Tair_min;Tair_max;Tfreecool;Tcombi;
fgw_precool;mgw:Tcond;Taircond_in;Tairfree_in;Jcond;Jfree;maircond_in;mairfree_in;mairfree_in_100;TairGWHEX2_in;
mairGWHEX2_in;mgwGWHEX1_in;mgwGWHEX2_in;mgwwell)
"Minimum condensing temperature"
If (Tair <= (Tcondmin-dTcond-dTdry)) Then
Tcond := Tcondmin
Taircond_in := Tcondmin - dTcond
==PAGE:104==
File:Reference system.EES
31-05-2017 18:31:26  Page 7
EES Ver. 10.207: #0780: Department of Energy Engineering, Tech. Univ. of Denmark
Else
Tcond := Tair + dTcond + dTdry
Taircond_in := Tair + dTdry
Endif
"Frost protection in free cooler and groundwater HEX 2"
If (Tair <= Tfreemin - dTdry) Then
Tairfree_in := Tfreemin
TairGWHEX2_in := Tfreemin
Else
Tairfree_in := Tair + dTdry
TairGWHEX2_in := Tair + dTdry
Endif
"Air mass flow rates"
If (opmode = 1) Then
If (Tair <= Tfreemin - dTdry) Then
Jcond := 0
Jfree := (89,48 - 22,38)[kg/s]/(Tfreecool - Tair_min)
maircond_in := 0
mairfree_in := 22,38[kg/s] + Jfree * ((Tfreemin - dTdry) - Tair_min)
mairfree_in_100 := 89,48
Else
Jcond := 0
Jfree := (89,48 - 22,38)[kg/s]/(Tfreecool - Tair_min)
maircond_in := 0[kg/s]
mairfree_in := 22,38[kg/s] + Jfree * (Tair - Tair_min)
mairfree_in_100 := 89,48[kg/s]
Endif
Else
 
If (opmode = 2) Then
Jcond := (49,21 - 9,843)[kg/s]/(Tcombi - Tfreecool)
Jfree := (22,37 - 89,48)[kg/s]/(Tcombi - Tfreecool)
maircond_in := 9,843[kg/s] + Jcond * (Tair - Tfreecool)
mairfree_in := 89,48[kg/s] + Jfree * (Tair - Tfreecool)
mairfree_in_100 := 89,48[kg/s]
Else
Jcond := (753,3 - 289,21)[kg/s]/(Tair_max - Tcombi)
Jfree := 0
maircond_in := 289,21[kg/s] + Jcond * (Tair - Tcombi)
mairfree_in := 0[kg/s]
mairfree_in_100 := 89,48[kg/s]
Endif
Endif
If (mode2$ = 'on') Then
"Condenser heat removal"
mairGWHEX2_in := 175 [kg/s]
Else
If (mode2$ = 'recharge') Then
mairGWHEX2_in := 100 [kg/s]
Else
mairGWHEX2_in := 0 [kg/s]
Endif
Endif
 
"! Mass flows"
If ((mode1$ = 'on') and (mode2$ = 'on')) Then
mgwGWHEX1_in := mgw * fgw_precool
mgwGWHEX2_in := mgw * (1 - fgw_precool)
mgwwell := mgw
Else
If ((mode1$ = 'on') and (mode2$ = 'off')) Then
mgwGWHEX1_in := mgw
mgwGWHEX2_in := 0
mgwwell := mgw
Else
If ((mode1$ = 'off') and ((mode2$ = 'on') or (mode2$ = 'recharge'))) Then
mgwGWHEX1_in := 0
mgwGWHEX2_in := mgw
mgwwell := mgw
Else 
==PAGE:105==
File:Reference system.EES
31-05-2017 18:31:26  Page 8
EES Ver. 10.207: #0780: Department of Energy Engineering, Tech. Univ. of Denmark
mgwGWHEX1_in := 0
mgwGWHEX2_in := 0
mgwwell := 0
Endif
 
Endif
Endif
End
 
// Procedure for groundwater flow.
Procedure gwflowconfig(mode1$;mode2$;mgw;Tgw_nat;Cgw_GWHEX2;Cair_GWHEX2;dT_GWHEX2;mairGWHEX2_in;
TairGWHEX2_in;cpair;cpgw;cpdc;mdcGWHEX1_in;TdcGWHEX1_in;Cgw_GWHEX1;Cdc_GWHEX1;dT_GWHEX1;
mgwGWHEX1_in;mgwGWHEX2_in;Vdotwell;kinvisc;pipe_dia;velocity_pipe:TgwGWHEX1_in;TgwGWHEX2_in;
TgwGWHEX1_out;TgwGWHEX2_out;QdotGWHEX1;QdotGWHEX2_cool;QdotGWHEX2_recharge;TdcGWHEX1_out;
TairGWHEX2_out;Vdotwell_current;Reynolds)
 
{Qaggr_cool :=  sumparametric('GW for peak load (recharge)';'Q_dot_GWHEX1';1;TableRun#-1)
Qaggr_recharge := sumparametric('GW for peak load (recharge)';'Q_dot_GWHEX2_recharge';1;TableRun#-1)}
 
"! Groundwater heat exchanger 2 (GW HEX 2)"
If (mode2$ = 'on') Then 
"Condenser heat removal"
If (Cgw_GWHEX2<=Cair_GWHEX2) Then 
"If C_gw < C_air then the pinch is at groundwater 
outlet."
TgwGWHEX2_in := Tgw_nat
TgwGWHEX2_out := TairGWHEX2_in - dT_GWHEX2
QdotGWHEX2_cool := mgwGWHEX2_in * cpgw * (TgwGWHEX2_out - TgwGWHEX2_in)
TairGWHEX2_out := TairGWHEX2_in - QdotGWHEX2_cool / (mairGWHEX2_in * cpair)
QdotGWHEX2_recharge := 0
Else 
"If C_gw > C_air then the pinch is at the 
groundwater inlet."
TgwGWHEX2_in := Tgw_nat
TairGWHEX2_out := TgwGWHEX2_in + dT_GWHEX2
QdotGWHEX2_cool := mairGWHEX2_in * cpair * (TairGWHEX2_in - TairGWHEX2_out)
TgwGWHEX2_out := TgwGWHEX2_in - QdotGWHEX2_cool / (mgwGWHEX2_in * cpgw)
QdotGWHEX2_recharge := 0
Endif
Else
If (mode2$ = 'recharge') Then
"Recharging groundwater - hot side of GW HEX 2 
is now groundwater"
TgwGWHEX2_in := 13,34[C]
TgwGWHEX2_out := 10,27[C]
QdotGWHEX2_recharge := mgwGWHEX2_in * cpgw * (TgwGWHEX2_in - TgwGWHEX2_out)
TairGWHEX2_out := TairGWHEX2_in + QdotGWHEX2_recharge / (mairGWHEX2_in * cpair)
QdotGWHEX2_cool := 0
Else
TgwGWHEX2_in := 999[C]
TgwGWHEX2_out := 999[C]
QdotGWHEX2_recharge := 0
TairGWHEX2_out := 999[C]
QdotGWHEX2_cool := 0
Endif
Endif
 
"! Groundwater heat exchanger 1 (GW HEX 1)"
If (mode1$ = 'on') Then
If (Cgw_GWHEX1<=Cdc_GWHEX1) Then 
"If C_gw < C_air then the pinch is at groundwater 
outlet."
TgwGWHEX1_in := Tgw_nat
TgwGWHEX1_out := TdcGWHEX1_in - dT_GWHEX1
QdotGWHEX1 := mgwGWHEX1_in * cpgw * (TgwGWHEX1_out - TgwGWHEX1_in)
TdcGWHEX1_out := TdcGWHEX1_in - QdotGWHEX1 / (mdcGWHEX1_in * cpdc)
Else
"If C_gw > C_air then the pinch is at the 
groundwater inlet."
TgwGWHEX1_in := Tgw_nat
TdcGWHEX1_out := TgwGWHEX1_in + dT_GWHEX1
QdotGWHEX1 := mdcGWHEX1_in * cpdc * (TdcGWHEX1_in - TdcGWHEX1_out)
TgwGWHEX1_out := TgwGWHEX1_in + QdotGWHEX1 / (mgwGWHEX1_in * cpgw)
Endif
Else
==PAGE:106==
File:Reference system.EES
31-05-2017 18:31:26  Page 9
EES Ver. 10.207: #0780: Department of Energy Engineering, Tech. Univ. of Denmark
TgwGWHEX1_in := 999
TgwGWHEX1_out := 999
QdotGWHEX1 := 0
TdcGWHEX1_out := 16
"Set to return temperature of DC distribution if GW 
HEX1 is not in use"
Endif
 
If ((QdotGWHEX1 > 0,1) or (QdotGWHEX2_cool > 0,1) or (QdotGWHEX2_recharge > 0,1)) Then
Vdotwell_current := Vdotwell
Else 
Vdotwell_current := 0
Endif
 
If ((mgwGWHEX1_in >= 0,1) or (mgwGWHEX2_in >=0,1)) Then
Reynolds := velocity_pipe * pipe_dia / kinvisc
Else 
Reynolds := 0,000000001
Endif
End 
 
// Procedure for different general outputs.
Procedure outputs(opmode;mode1$;mode2$;Wcomp;Wfans_cond;Wfans_free;Wfans_GWHEX2;Wpump_dc_evap;
Wpump_cond;Wpump_free;Wpump_GWHEX2;Wpump_gw;Wpump_dc_gw;Wpump_dc_free;Qevap;Qfree;Qgw;
Wdotpump_dist:cop;cop_mech;cop_free;cop_gw)
If (opmode = 1) Then
If (mode1$ = 'on') Then
cop := (Qfree + Qgw) / (Wfans_free + Wpump_free + Wpump_gw + Wpump_dc_free + Wpump_dc_gw + 
Wdotpump_dist)
cop_mech := 0
cop_free := Qfree / (Wfans_free + Wpump_free + Wpump_dc_free)
cop_gw := Qgw / (Wpump_gw + Wpump_dc_gw)
Else
cop := Qfree / (Wfans_free + Wpump_free + Wpump_dc_free + Wpump_gw + Wpump_GWHEX2 + Wfans_GWHEX2 
+ Wdotpump_dist)
cop_mech := 0
cop_free := Qfree / (Wfans_free + Wpump_free + Wpump_dc_free)
cop_gw := 0
Endif
Else
If (opmode = 2) Then
If (mode1$ = 'on') Then
cop := (Qfree + Qgw + Qevap) / (Wfans_free + Wpump_free + Wpump_dc_free + Wpump_gw + Wpump_dc_gw + 
Wcomp + Wfans_cond + Wpump_cond + Wpump_dc_evap + Wdotpump_dist)
cop_mech := Qevap / (Wcomp + Wfans_cond + Wpump_cond + Wpump_dc_evap)
cop_free := Qfree / (Wfans_free + Wpump_free + Wpump_dc_free)
cop_gw := Qgw / (Wpump_gw + Wpump_dc_gw)
Else
cop := (Qfree + Qevap) / (Wfans_free + Wpump_free + Wpump_dc_free + Wpump_gw + Wcomp + Wfans_cond + 
Wpump_cond + Wpump_dc_evap + Wpump_GWHEX2 + Wfans_GWHEX2 + Wdotpump_dist)
cop_mech := Qevap / (Wcomp + Wfans_cond + Wpump_cond + Wpump_dc_evap)
cop_free := Qfree / (Wfans_free + Wpump_free + Wpump_dc_free)
cop_gw := 0
Endif
Else
If (mode1$ = 'on') Then
cop :=  (Qgw + Qevap) / (Wpump_gw + Wpump_dc_gw + Wcomp + Wfans_cond + Wpump_cond + Wpump_dc_evap 
+ Wdotpump_dist)
cop_mech := Qevap / Wcomp
cop_free := 0
cop_gw := Qgw / (Wpump_gw + Wpump_dc_gw) 
Else 
cop := Qevap / (Wpump_gw + Wcomp + Wfans_cond + Wpump_cond + Wpump_dc_evap + Wpump_GWHEX2 + 
Wfans_GWHEX2 + Wdotpump_dist)
cop_mech := Qevap / (Wcomp + Wfans_cond + Wpump_cond + Wpump_dc_evap)
cop_free := 0
cop_gw := 0
Endif
Endif
==PAGE:107==
File:Reference system.EES
31-05-2017 18:31:26  Page 10
EES Ver. 10.207: #0780: Department of Energy Engineering, Tech. Univ. of Denmark
Endif
End 
 
// Procedure for checking pinch in condenser.
Procedure pinchcheck(opmode;Q61;T65;T64;Q65;Q64:Q67;const;T67)
If (opmode = 1) Then
Q67 := 1
const := 1
T67 := 1
Else
If (opmode = 2) Then
Q67 := Q61
const := (T65 - T64) / (Q65 - Q64)
T67 := T64 + Q67 * const
Else
Q67 := Q61
const := (T65 - T64) / (Q65 - Q64)
T67 := T64 + Q67 * const
Endif
Endif
End 
 
// Procedure to determine the conditions at which overall operation mode changes
Procedure oplimits(TDC_sup;TDC_ret;mode1$;dTdry;dTfree;TDCprecool_min:Tfreecool;Tcombi)
If (mode1$ = 'on') Then
Tfreecool = TDC_sup - dTdry - dTfree 
"At T_air <= T_freecool the operation mode will be 
free cooling. At T_air > T_freecool the operation mode will be combi cooling."
Tcombi = TDCprecool_min - dTdry - dTfree 
"At T_air <= T_combi the operation mode will be 
combi cooling. At T_air > T_combi the operation mode will be only mechanical."
Else
Tfreecool = TDC_sup - dTdry - dTfree
Tcombi = TDC_ret - dTdry - dTfree
Endif
End

"Assumed pressure loss in suction line"

"Atmospheric pressure"

P_gw = 1,0 [bar]
"Pressure of groundwater in aquifer"
P_gw_ATES = 2,1 [bar]
"Pressure of groundwater in the ATES pipe system"
DELTAT_GWHEX1 = 2,5 [K]
"Pinch point temperature difference in groundwater heat exchangers"
DELTAT_GWHEX2 = 2,5 [K]

well"
// Design conditions
Q_dot_dist_100 = 5910 [kW]
"District cooling demand, design condition (maximum)"
h_DC_ret_100 = enthalpy(D$;T=T_DC_ret;P=P_DC_ret) "Enthalpy of DC return water, design condition"
h_DC_sup_100 = enthalpy(D$;T=T_DC_sup;P=P_DC_sup) "Enthalpy of DC supply water, design condition"
Q_dot_dist_100 = m_dot_dist_100 * (h_DC_ret_100 - h_DC_sup_100) "Gives the mass flow rate of DC water, design 
condition"
Q_dot_dry_100 = 7701 [kW]
"Dry cooler capacity at design conditions (100% capacity)"
V_dot_air_100 = 2330989 [m^3/h]
"Dry cooler volume flow rate at design conditions (100% capacity)"
f_fans = 0,03 [-]
"Fan power consumption fraction of design capacity (typical value). Reference: 
PackCalc"
W_dot_fans_100 = f_fans * Q_dot_dry_100 "Fan power at design conditions (100% capacity)"
//UA-values for heat exchangers. Calculated separately on the basis of a given design condition.
UA_evap_100 = 637,2 [kW/K]
"Assumed pinch=5K, at design condition T_air=32,1C and Q_demand = 5910kW"
UA_evap = UA_evap_100 * (m_dot_dist/m_dot_dist_100)^0,8 "UA value of evaporator is variable with the mass flow rate 
on DC water side, which is assumed to be the dominating side with respect to change in the overall heat transfer 
coefficient."
 
// Ambient air temperature - hourly data from temperature profile
"ParametricTable keyword returns true if solved from Parametric Table, and false when solved from Equations Window. 
Embedded in and if-else statement, both options are available in the code without out-commenting any variables. The 
average temperature from DRY is 8.6 C."
$If ParametricTable
$Elseif 
T_air = 32,1 [C]
$Endif
 
// Demand - hourly data from demand profile
"When the system of equations are solved from the Equations Window, the maximum value of demand profile is used. 
When solved from the Parametric Table, calculations will be performed for each hour in the year, using values from 
demand profile."
$If ParametricTable
$ElseIf
Q_dot_dist = 5910 [kW]
hour = 0
"Does not influence any calculations"
$Endif 
{hour = 0}
// Natural groundwater temperature
T_gw_min = 9,7 [C]
"Minimum groundwater temperature over the year"

mode_GWHEX1$ = 'off'

//_______________________________ STATE POINT EVALUATION _____________________________________
//*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-
 
// DC WATER SYSTEM
"State 24"
T[24] = T_DC_ret
"Return temperature of DC distribution is 
predefined"
P[24] = P_DC_ret
"Return pressure of DC distribution is predefined"
h[24] = enthalpy(D$;T=T[24];P=P[24])
 
"Enthalpy of DC 
return water"
"State 25"
T[25] = T_DC_sup
"Supply temperature of DC distribution is 
predefined"
P[25] = P_DC_sup
"Supply pressure of DC distribution is predefined"
h[25] = enthalpy(D$;T=T[25];P=P[25])
 
"Enthalpy of DC 
supply water"
Q_dot_dist = m_dot_dist * (h[24] - h[25])
"Cooling energy supplied to the network is given by 
demand curve. This determines mass flow on distribution network." 
"State 31"
C_hot_free = m_dot_31 * cp_31
"Capacity stream of DC distribution water in the 
free cooler"
f_pump = 0,0015 [1/K]
"Typical const. value for pump power rel., Granryd (
1998)"
W_dot_pump_dc_free = Q_dot_free * f_pump * (T[31] - T[32])
"Pump power for primary pumps contribution to 
flow in free cooler. Granryd (1998)"
"State 39"
W_dot_pump_dc_evap = Q_dot_evap * f_pump * (T[41] - T[42])
"Pump power for primary pumps contribution to 
flow in evaporator. Granryd (1998)"
"State 41"
m_dot_41 = m_dot_39
T[41] = T[39]
P[41] = P[39]
h[41] = enthalpy(D$;T=T[41];P=P[41])
"Enthalpy of DC 
distribution water into evaporator"
"State 44"
T_setpoint = T_DC_sup
"Set point temperature defined"
T[44] = T_setpoint
"Temperature before distribution pumps 
corresponds to set point"
P[44] = P_DC_ret
"Pressure is assumed to be equal to distribution 
return"
==PAGE:110==
File:Reference system.EES
31-05-2017 18:31:26  Page 13
EES Ver. 10.207: #0780: Department of Energy Engineering, Tech. Univ. of Denmark
h[44] = enthalpy(D$;T=T[44];P=P[44])
"Enthalpy of 
before distribution pumps"
v_44 = volume(D$;T=T[44];P=P[44])
"Specific volume before distribution pumps"
V_dot_dist = m_dot_dist * v_44
"Volume flow rate before distribution pumps in [m^
3/s]"
W_dot_pump_dist = V_dot_dist * (P[45]*convert(bar;kPa) - P[44]*convert(bar;kPa)) / eta_tot_pump "Power of distribution 
pumps"
"State 45"
T[45] = T[44]
"Temperature after distribution pumps"
P[45] = P_DC_sup
"Pressure after distribution pumps"
h[45] = enthalpy(D$;T=T[45];P=P[45])
"Enthalpy after 
distribution pumps"
"State 47"
cp_47 = cp(D$;T=T_DC_ret;P=P_DC_ret)
"Specific heat capacity of distribution water into pre-
cooler (GW HEX 1)"
C_dc_GWHEX1 = cp_47 * m_dot_47
"Capacity stream 
of distribution side in pre-cooler (GW HEX 1)"
W_dot_pump_dc_gw = Q_dot_GWHEX1 * f_pump * (T[47] - T[48])
"Pump power for primary pumps contribution to 
flow in pre-cooler (GW HEX 1). Granryd (1998)"
 
// AIR SIDE
"State 9"
T[9] = T_air
"Ambient air temperature"
P[9] = P_atm
"Ambient pressure assumed to be atmospheric"
h[9] = enthalpy(A$;T=T[9];P=P[9])
"Enthalpy of ambient air"
m_dot_air_tot = m_dot_16 + m_dot_10 + m_dot_96
"Total mass flow of air through dry coolers"
v_9 = volume(A$;T=T[9];P=P[9])
"Specific volume of ambient air"
cp_air = cp(A$;T=T[9];P=P[9])
"Specific heat capacity of ambient air"
"State 99"
Q_dot_dry = Q_dot_free + Q_dot_cond + Q_dot_GWHEX2_cool + Q_dot_GWHEX2_recharge "Total dry cooler load"
V_dot_air_tot = V_dot_16 + V_dot_10 + V_dot_96
"Total volume flow of air through dry coolers"
CAP_fans = V_dot_air_tot / V_dot_air_100
"Capacity of variable speed fans"
W_dot_fans = W_dot_fans_100 * CAP_fans^2,8
"Total fan power"
"State 10 (assumed to be air)"
P[10] = P[9]
"Pressure equals ambient"
h[10] = enthalpy(A$;T=T[10];P=P[10])
"Enthalpy of air 
entering condenser"
v_10 = volume(A$;T=T[10];P=P[10])
"Specific volume of air entering the condenser"
V_dot_10 = m_dot_10 * convert(kg/s;kg/h) * v_10
"Conversion from mass flow to volume flow"
cp_10 = cp(A$;T=T[10];h=h[10])
"Specific heat capacity of air into the condenser"
W_dot_pump_cond = Q_dot_cond * f_pump * (T[11] - T[10])
"Pump power for brine pumps contribution to flow 
in condenser. Granryd (1998)"
W_dot_fans_cond = V_dot_10/V_dot_air_tot * W_dot_fans
"Fan power contribution to condenser"
"State 11 (assumed to be air)"
P[11] = P[10]
"Pressure of air assumed unchanged over the 
condenser"
h[11] = enthalpy(A$;T=T[11];P=P[11])
"Enthalpy of air 
out of the condenser"
"State 16 (assumed to be air)" 
P[16] = P[9]
"Pressure equals ambient"
h[16] = enthalpy(A$;T=T[16];P=P[16])
"Enthalpy of air 
entering free cooler"
v_16 = volume(A$;T=T[16];P=P[16])
"Specific volume of air entering the free cooler"
V_dot_16 = m_dot_16 * convert(kg/s;kg/h) * v_16
"Conversion from mass flow to volume flow"
cp_16 = cp(A$;T=T[16];h=h[16])
"Specific heat capacity of air into the free cooler"
C_cold_free = m_dot_16 * cp_16
"Capacity stream of air into the free cooler"
W_dot_pump_free = Q_dot_free * f_pump * (T[17] - T[16])
"Pump power for brine pumps contribution to flow 
in free cooler. Granryd (1998)"
W_dot_fans_free = V_dot_16/V_dot_air_tot * W_dot_fans
"Fan power contribution to free cooler"
"State 17 (assumed to be air)"
P[17] = P[16]
"Pressure of air assumed unchanged over the free 
cooler"
h[17] = enthalpy(A$;T=T[17];P=P[17])
"Enthalpy of air 
out of the free cooler"
"State 96 (assumed to be air)"
P[96] = P[9]
"Pressure equals ambient"
h[96] = enthalpy(A$;T=T[96];P=P[96])
"Enthalpy of air 
entering the GW HEX 2"
==PAGE:111==
File:Reference system.EES
31-05-2017 18:31:26  Page 14
EES Ver. 10.207: #0780: Department of Energy Engineering, Tech. Univ. of Denmark
v_96 = volume(A$;T=T[96];P=P[96])
"Specific volume of air entering GW HEX 2"
V_dot_96 = m_dot_96 * convert(kg/s;kg/h) * v_96
"Conversion from mass flow to volume flow"
cp_96 = cp(A$;T=T[96];h=h[96])
"Specific heat capacity of air into GW HEX 2"
C_air_GWHEX2 = m_dot_96 * cp_96
"Capacity stream 
of air into GW HEX 2)"
W_dot_pump_GWHEX2 = (Q_dot_GWHEX2_cool + Q_dot_GWHEX2_recharge) * f_pump * abs(T[97] - T[96]) "Pump 
power for brine pumps contribution to flow in GW HEX 2. Granryd (1998)"
W_dot_fans_GWHEX2 = V_dot_96/V_dot_air_tot * W_dot_fans
"Fan power contribution to GW HEX 2"
"State 97 (assumed to be air)"
P[97] = P[96]
"Pressure of air assumed unchanged over GW 
HEX 2"
h[97] = enthalpy(A$;T=T[97];P=P[97]) 
"Enthalpy of air out of GW HEX 2"
 
// GROUNDWATER SIDE
"State 76"
P[76] = P[82]
"ATES system pressure"
v_76 = volume(G$;T=T[76];P=P[76])
"Specific volume of groundwater into GW HEX 2"
C_gw_GWHEX2 = cp_gw * m_dot_76
"Capacity stream 
of groundwater into GW HEX 2"
V_dot_76 = m_dot_76*convert(kg/s;kg/h) * v_76
"Conversion of mass flow to volume flow"
"State 78"
P[78] = P[82]
"ATES system pressure"
v_78 = volume(G$;T=T[78];P=P[78])
"Specific volume of groundwater into GW HEX 1"
C_gw_GWHEX1 = cp_gw * m_dot_78 
"Capacity stream of groundwater into GW HEX 1"
V_dot_78 = m_dot_78*convert(kg/s;kg/h) * v_78
"Conversion of mass flow to volume flow"
"State 81"
conv_kPa_m = 0,102 [m/kPa]
"Conversion from pressure (kPa) to head (m)"
conv_bartom = 10,2 [m/bar]
"Conversion from pressure (bar) to head (m)"
PL = 2 [m]
"Plant Level - plant height above ground (assumed)
"
TWL = -4,21 [m]
"Top Water Level - highest groundwater level (
assumed)"
BWL = -14 [m]
"Bottom Water Level - lowest groundwater level"
H_S_min = PL - TWL
"Minimum static head"
H_S_max = PL - BWL
"Maximum static head"
D_pipe = 0,2 [m]
"Assumed diameter of groundwater pipes"
L_pipe = 500 [m]
"Assumed total pipe length for one well pair"
A_pipe = PI * D_pipe^2 / 4
"Cross sectional area of grundwater pipe"
vel_gw = V_dot_well*convert(m^3/h;m^3/s)/A_pipe
"Mean velocity in the ground water pipe"
K_fittings = 23,64 [-]
"Loss coeff. for friction loss in valves, bends etc."
e_PE = 0,000005 * convert(ft;m)
"Roughness for pipe inner surface - assumed to be 
PE"
nu_gw = kinematicviscosity(G$;T=T[82];P=P[82])
"Kinematic viscosity of groundwater"
Arg = e_PE/(3,7*D_pipe)+5,74/Re_gw^0,9
"Argument for logarithmic calculation for friction 
factor"
fric_pipe = 0,25 / (log10(Arg))^2
"Friction factor. Based on roughn., pipe dia. and 
Reynolds num."
K_pipe = fric_pipe * L_pipe / D_pipe
"Loss coeff. for surface friction along the lenght of 
pipes"
K_tot = K_fittings + K_pipe
"Total loss coefficient"
g = 9,81 [m/s^2]
"Acceleration due to gravity"
H_D = K_tot * vel_gw^2 / (2*g)
"Dynamic head"
H_tot_max = H_S_max + H_D + (P_gw_ATES - P_gw)*conv_bartom
"Total head for the pump to overcome, worst case"
H_tot_min = H_S_min + H_D + (P_gw_ATES - P_gw)*conv_bartom
"Total head for the pump to overcome, best case"
rho_gw = density(G$;T=T_gw_nat;x=0)
"Density of groundwater"
W_dot_pump_well = V_dot_well_current*convert(m^3/h;m^3/s) * H_tot_max * g * rho_gw / eta_tot_pump_ATES / 1000[W/
kW] "Required groundwater pump power input for 1 well pair"
W_dot_pump_gw_tot = n_gw_pairs * W_dot_pump_well 
"Total required groundwater pump power input"
"State 82"
T[82] = T_gw_nat
"Natural ground water temperature in for cooling. 
Not used under recharge."
P[82] = P_gw_ATES
"Assumed pressure level in the ATES system"
cp_gw = cp(G$;T=T[82];P=P[82])
"Specific heat of groundwater"
v_82 = volume(G$;T=T[82];P=P[82])
"Specific volume of groundwater"
m_dot_gw = V_dot_gw*convert(m^3/h;m^3/s) / v_82
"Conversion from volume flow to mass flow. 
Nominal value."
V_dot_82 = m_dot_82*convert(kg/s;kg/h) * v_82
"Conversion from mass flow to volume flow"

"! COOLING PLANT WITH ATES - PEAK LOAD OPERATION"
$TabStops 0,5 5 cm
$UNITSYSTEM SI C bar kJ
$UpdateGuesses
 
//_____________________________________ SUBPROGRAMS ________________________________________
//*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-
// Subprogam for free cooling HEX (operation mode: free cooling).
Subprogram freehex(Tairfree_in;Tdcfree_in;Pdc_in;Tset;mdc;cpair_in;mairfree_in:Tdc_out_final;cpdc_in;Qdot_free;
Tairfree_out)
$UpdateGuesses
"Mediums"
D$ = 'water'
"Air side"
Qdot_free = mairfree_in * cpair_in * (Tairfree_out - Tairfree_in)
"DC water inlet"
cpdc_in = cp(D$;T=Tdcfree_in;P=Pdc_in)
"Specific heat capacity of DC inlet water"
"DC water outlet"
Qdot_free = mdc * cpdc_in * (Tdcfree_in - Tset)
"Temperature based heat transfer rate, based on 
DC-side"
Tdc_out_final = Tset
"Assigning output-value for DC-out state"
End
 
// Subprogam for free cooling HEX and chiller cycle (operation mode: combi).
Subprogram freehexchiller(Taircond_in;Tairfree_in;Tcond;UAevap;mdc;Tdcfree_in;Pdc_in;etacomp;dTsc;dTsh;Tset;
cpair_in;mairfree_in;maircond_in;Tdc_inter;xevap_out;dp_sl;etamotor:Qdot_cond;Taircond_out;DELTAT_1evap;Tevap;
DELTAT_2evap;DELTAT_CMevap;Qdot_evap;Pevap;Tsuction;Psuction;hsuction;ssuction;Pdischarge;sisdischarge;
hisdischarge;hdischarge;Tdischarge;mrefrigerant;hcondensate;Wdot_comp;Pratio;Pcond;Tcondensate;Pcondensate;
Texpand;Pexpand;hexpand;Tdcevap_out;cpdcevap_out;hevap_out;ncirc;Tevap_out;Pevap_out;mevap;hevap_sat_l;
hevap_sat_v;Tevap_sat_l;Pevap_sat_l;Tevap_sat_v;Pevap_sat_v)
$UpdateGuesses
"Mediums"
RE$ = 'Ammonia'
D$ = 'Water'
 
"! *_*_*_*_*_*_*_* Free cooler *_*_*_*_*_*_*_*"
"Free cooler calculations for combi mode are moved outside the subprogram. Find the equations in procedure 
activecomponents."
 
"! *_*_*_*_*_*_*_* Chiller *_*_*_*_*_*_*_*"
"Condenser air inlet"
Qdot_cond = maircond_in * cpair_in * (Taircond_out-Taircond_in) 
"Eq. for condenser heat gives the brine temp. after 
condenser"
 
"Evaporator"
DELTAT_1evap = Tdc_inter - Tevap
"Temperature difference, hot end"
DELTAT_2evap = Tdcevap_out - Tevap
"Temperature difference, cold end"
"Chen mean (CMTD)"
DELTAT_CMevap = (1/2*DELTAT_1evap^0,3275 + 1/2*DELTAT_2evap^0,3275)^(1/0,3275)
Qdot_evap = UAevap * DELTAT_CMevap
Pevap = pressure(RE$;T=Tevap;x=1)
"Evaporation 
pressure defined from refrigerant saturated state"
hevap_out = enthalpy(RE$;T=Tevap;x=xevap_out)
"Enthalpy of refrigerant out of evaporator (
assumed quality <1 for the flooded evaporator)"
ncirc = 1/xevap_out
"Circulation number in flooded evaporator"
Tevap_out = Tevap
"Temperature out of the evaporator corresponds to 
evaporation temperature"
Pevap_out = Pevap
"Pressure out of the evaporator corresponds to 
evaporation temperature"
"Low pressure receiver"
hevap_sat_l = enthalpy(RE$;T=Tevap;x=0)
"Enthapy of saturated liquid in the receiver"
Tevap_sat_l = Tevap
Pevap_sat_l = Pevap
hevap_sat_v = enthalpy(RE$;T=Tevap;x=1)
"Enthapy of saturated vapor in the receiver"
Tevap_sat_v = Tevap
Pevap_sat_v = Pevap
Qdot_evap = mevap/ncirc * (hevap_sat_v - hevap_sat_l)
"Equation for heat rate in flooded evaporator gives 
the actual mass flow of liquid refrigerant in the evaporator"
==PAGE:120==
File:ATES peak 1500.EES
31-05-2017 19:18:47  Page 3
EES Ver. 10.207: #0780: Department of Energy Engineering, Tech. Univ. of Denmark
"Compressor suction side"
Tsuction = Tevap_out + dTsh
"Temperature before compressor - super heat is 
unuseful (supplied to the refrigerant in suction line from compressor heat etc.)"
Psuction = Pevap - dp_sl
"Pressure before compressor equals evaporation 
pressure minus assumed pressure loss in suction line"
hsuction = enthalpy(RE$;T=Tsuction;P=Psuction)
"Enthalpy of superheated refrigerant after 
evaporator"
ssuction = entropy(RE$;T=Tsuction;P=Psuction)
"Entropy before compressor"
"Compressor discharge side"
Pdischarge = Pcond
"Comp. applies a press. rise corresp. to necessary 
cond. pressure"
sisdischarge = ssuction
"Isentropic compression"
hisdischarge = enthalpy(RE$;s=sisdischarge;P=Pdischarge) 
"Enthalpy in the case of isentropic compression"
etacomp = (hisdischarge-hsuction)/(hdischarge-hsuction) 
"Expression for isentropic efficiency used to 
dertermine actual enthalpy after compressor."
Tdischarge = temperature(RE$;h=hdischarge;P=Pdischarge) 
"Refrigerant temperature out of condenser"
Qdot_cond = mrefrigerant * (hdischarge - hcondensate)
"Calculation of heat rejection in the condenser"
Wdot_comp = mrefrigerant * (hdischarge - hsuction)/etamotor
"Compressor power"
Pratio = Pdischarge/Psuction
"Pressure ratio"
"Condensate out of condenser"
Pcond = pressure(RE$;T=Tcond;x=1) 
"Condensation pressure"
Tcondensate = Tcond - dTsc
"Refrigerant temp. out of condenser is cond. temp. 
minus subcool."
Pcondensate = Pcond
"Refrigerant press. out of condenser is the cond. 
pressure"
hcondensate = enthalpy(RE$;T=Tcondensate;P=Pcondensate) 
"Enthalpy out of the condenser"
"Expanded condensate before evaporator"
Texpand = Tevap
"Refrigerant temp. into evaporator is the 
evaporation temp."
Pexpand = Pevap
"Refrigerant pressure into evaporator is the 
evaporation pressure"
hexpand = hcondensate
"Isenthalpic expansion: Enthalpy is unchanged 
over the exp. valve"
Qdot_evap = mrefrigerant * (hsuction - hexpand)
"Eq. for energy transfer in the evaporator gives 
mass flow on refrigerant side"
"DC water after evaporator"
Tdcevap_out = Tset
"Chiller production controlled from setpoint DC 
supply temp."
cpdcevap_out = cp(D$;T=Tdcevap_out;P=Pdc_in)
"Specific heat of of chilled water out of evaporator"
Qdot_evap = mdc * cpdcevap_out * (Tdc_inter - Tdcevap_out) 
"Calculation of required cooling delivered by 
evaporator"
 
End
 
 
// Subprogram for chiller cycle.
Subprogram chiller(maircond_in;cpair_in;Taircond_in;Tdcevap_in;UAevap;dTsh;etacomp;dTsc;Tset;Pdcevap_in;mdc;
Tcond;xevap_out;dp_sl;etamotor:Qdot_cond;Taircond_out;DELTAT_1evap;Tdcevap_out;DELTAT_2evap;Tevap;
DELTAT_CMevap;Qdot_evap;Pevap;Tsuction;Psuction;hsuction;ssuction;Pdischarge;sisdischarge;hisdischarge;
hdischarge;Tdischarge;mrefrigerant;hcondensate;Wdot_comp;Pratio;Pcond;Tcondensate;Pcondensate;Texpand;
Pexpand;hexpand;cpdcevap_out;hevap_out;ncirc;Tevap_out;Pevap_out;mevap;hevap_sat_l;hevap_sat_v;Tevap_sat_l;
Pevap_sat_l;Tevap_sat_v;Pevap_sat_v)
$UpdateGuesses
RE$ = 'Ammonia'
D$ = 'Water'
 
"Condenser air inlet"
Qdot_cond = maircond_in * cpair_in * (Taircond_out-Taircond_in) 
"Eq. for condenser heat gives the brine temp. after 
condenser"
"Evaporator"
DELTAT_1evap = Tdcevap_in - Tevap
"Temperature 
difference, hot end"
DELTAT_2evap = Tdcevap_out - Tevap
"Temperature difference, cold end"
"Chen mean (CMTD)"
DELTAT_CMevap = (1/2*DELTAT_1evap^0,3275 + 1/2*DELTAT_2evap^0,3275)^(1/0,3275)
Qdot_evap = UAevap * DELTAT_CMevap
Pevap = pressure(RE$;T=Tevap;x=1)
"Evaporation 
pressure defined from refrigerant saturated state"
==PAGE:121==
File:ATES peak 1500.EES

//______________________________________ PROCEDURES _________________________________________
//*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-
 
// Procedure for definition of operation mode. Inputs: 'x'=determining temperature, 'tlow'=low operation mode limit, 'thigh'=
high operation mode limit, 'a'=first operation mode number, 'b'=second operation mode number, 'c'=third operation mode 
number. Output: 'name'=variable name of the (numeric) operation mode number. 
Procedure plantoperation(x;tlow;thigh;a;b;c:name)
==PAGE:122==
File:ATES peak 1500.EES
31-05-2017 19:18:47  Page 5
EES Ver. 10.207: #0780: Department of Energy Engineering, Tech. Univ. of Denmark
If (x <= tlow) Then
"Free cooling"
name := a
Else
"Combi cooling"
If (x <= thigh) Then
name := b
Else
"Mechanical cooling"
name := c
Endif
Endif
End
 
// Procedure that contains a condition for which components to be active in the cooling plant. The relevant subprograms 
are called according to the operation mode.
Procedure activecomponents(opmode;T[16];T[31];P[31];T_setpoint;m_dot_dist;cp_air;m_dot_16;T[10];T_cond;UA_evap;
eta_comp;DELTAT_sc;DELTAT_sh;m_dot_10;T[41];P[41];C_hot_free;C_cold_free;x_evap_out;DELTAp_sl;
eta_motor_comp:cp_31;Q_dot_free;T[17];T[32];Q_dot_cond;T[11];DELTAT_1_evap;DELTAT_2_evap;T_evap;
DELTAT_CM_evap;Q_dot_evap;P_evap;T[1];P[1];h[1];s_1;P[2];s_2_s;h_2_s;h[2];T[2];m_dot_r;h[3];W_dot_comp;P_rat;
P_cond;T[3];P[3];T[4];P[4];h[4];T[42];cp_42;h[6];n_circ;T[6];P[6];m_dot_evap;h[5];h[7];T[5];P[5];T[7];P[7])
 
If (opmode = 1) Then
"Free cooling"
Call freehex(T[16];T[31];P[31];T_setpoint;m_dot_dist;cp_air;m_dot_16:T[32];cp_31;Q_dot_free;T[17])
Q_dot_cond := 0
T[11] := T[10]
DELTAT_1_evap := 12,5
DELTAT_2_evap := 2
T_evap := 0
DELTAT_CM_evap := 5,725359747
Q_dot_evap := 0
P_evap := 4
T[1] := 5,5
P[1] := 4
h[1] := 0
s_1 := 0
P[2] := 8
s_2_s := 0
h_2_s := 0
h[2] := 0
T[2] := 20
m_dot_r := 0
h[3] := 0
W_dot_comp := 0
P_rat := 2
P_cond := 8
T[3] := 20
P[3] := 8
T[4] := 10
P[4] := 4
h[4] := 0
T[42] := 10
cp_42 := 4,183
h[6] := 0
n_circ:= 0
T[6] := 5,5
P[6] := 4
m_dot_evap := 0
h[5] := 0
h[7] = 0
T[5] := 0
P[5] := 0
T[7] := 0
P[7] := 0
Else
"Combi cooling"
If (opmode = 2) Then
==PAGE:123==
File:ATES peak 1500.EES
31-05-2017 19:18:47  Page 6
EES Ver. 10.207: #0780: Department of Energy Engineering, Tech. Univ. of Denmark
If (C_hot_free<=C_cold_free) Then
"If C_dc < C_air 
then the pinch is at DC water outlet."
T[32] := T[16] + 2,5[C]
cp_31 := 4,183[kJ/kg-K]
Q_dot_free := m_dot_dist * cp_31 * (T[31] - T[32])
T[17] := Q_dot_free / (m_dot_16 * cp_air) + T[16]
Else
"If C_dc > C_air then the pinch is at the DC water 
inlet."
T[17] := T[31] - 2,5[C]
cp_31 := 4,183[kJ/kg-K]
Q_dot_free := m_dot_16 * cp_air * (T[17] - T[16])
T[32] := T[31] - Q_dot_free / (m_dot_dist * cp_31)
Endif
 
Call freehexchiller(T[10];T[16];T_cond;UA_evap;m_dot_dist;T[31];P[31];eta_comp;DELTAT_sc;DELTAT_sh;T_setpoint;
cp_air;m_dot_16;m_dot_10;T[32];x_evap_out;DELTAp_sl;eta_motor_comp:Q_dot_cond;T[11];DELTAT_1_evap;T_evap;
DELTAT_2_evap;DELTAT_CM_evap;Q_dot_evap;P_evap;T[1];P[1];h[1];s_1;P[2];s_2_s;h_2_s;h[2];T[2];m_dot_r;h[3];
W_dot_comp;P_rat;P_cond;T[3];P[3];T[4];P[4];h[4];T[42];cp_42;h[6];n_circ;T[6];P[6];m_dot_evap;h[5];h[7];T[5];P[5];T[7];
P[7])
 
Else
"Mechanical cooling"
Call chiller(m_dot_10;cp_air;T[10];T[41];UA_evap;DELTAT_sh;eta_comp;DELTAT_sc;T_setpoint;P[41];m_dot_dist;
T_cond;x_evap_out;DELTAp_sl;eta_motor_comp:Q_dot_cond;T[11];DELTAT_1_evap;T[42];DELTAT_2_evap;T_evap;
DELTAT_CM_evap;Q_dot_evap;P_evap;T[1];P[1];h[1];s_1;P[2];s_2_s;h_2_s;h[2];T[2];m_dot_r;h[3];W_dot_comp;P_rat;
P_cond;T[3];P[3];T[4];P[4];h[4];cp_42;h[6];n_circ;T[6];P[6];m_dot_evap;h[5];h[7];T[5];P[5];T[7];P[7])
T[32] := 20
cp_31 := 4,183
Q_dot_free := 0
T[17] := T[16]
Endif
Endif
End
 
// Procedure for correct flow configuration of DC water according to the operation mode. 'final' refers to the state right 
before distribution pumps.
Procedure dcflowconfig(opmode;mdc_ret;Tdc_ret;Tdc_final;Tdcfree_out;Pdc_ret;mode1$;Tdc_precool:mdcGWHEX1;
mdcfree_in;mdcbuffer_in;mdcbuffer_out;mdcevap_in;mdcfinal;TdcGWHEX1_in;Tdcfree_in;Tdcbuffer_in;Tdcbuffer_out;
Tdcevap_in;Pdcfree_in;Pdcbuffer_in;Pdcbuffer_out;Pdcevap_in)
If (opmode = 1) Then
"! Statements for operation mode 1"
"Mass flow rates"
If (mode1$ = 'on') Then
mdcGWHEX1 := mdc_ret
Else
mdcGWHEX1 := 0
Endif
mdcfree_in := mdc_ret
mdcbuffer_in := mdcfree_in
mdcbuffer_out :=mdcbuffer_in

mdcfinal := mdcbuffer_out
 
"Temperatures"
If (mode1$ = 'on') Then
TdcGWHEX1_in := Tdc_ret
Tdcfree_in := Tdc_precool
Else
TdcGWHEX1_in := 999
Tdcfree_in := Tdc_ret
Endif
Tdcbuffer_in := Tdcfree_out
Tdcbuffer_out := Tdcbuffer_in
Tdcevap_in := 0
"Pressures"
Pdcfree_in := Pdc_ret
Pdcbuffer_in := Pdcfree_in
Pdcbuffer_out := Pdcbuffer_in
Pdcevap_in := 1

Else
If (opmode = 2) Then
"! Statements for operation mode 2"
"Mass flow rates"
If (mode1$ = 'on') Then
mdcGWHEX1 := mdc_ret
Else
mdcGWHEX1 := 0
Endif
mdcfree_in := mdc_ret
mdcbuffer_in := 0
mdcbuffer_out := 0
mdcevap_in := mdcfree_in
mdcfinal := mdcevap_in
 "Temperatures"
If (mode1$ = 'on') Then
TdcGWHEX1_in := Tdc_ret
Tdcfree_in := Tdc_precool
Else
